The function restores PCI state, re-enables the device, then calls azx_init_chip. The problem might be that polling_mode persists across the suspend/resume boundary without being cleared, causing subsequent command I/O operations to use the wrong communication method. addr));\n    \n    // initialize all streams\n    azx_init_stream(chip);\n    \n    // program the wallclock\n    azx_writel(chip, WALLCLK, 0);\n    \n    // delay\n    udelay(50);\n    \n    chip->initialized = 1;\n}\n```\n\nSo the issue is clear: when azx_init_chip is called with full_reset=1, it checks if chip->initialized is already 1 and returns early. But chip->initialized was set to 1 at the end of the previous azx_init_chip call. So on resume, azx_init_chip returns immediately without doing any initialization.\n\nThe fix would be to either:\n1. Reset chip->initialized = 0 before calling azx_init_chip on resume\n2. Pass a flag to azx_init_chip to force initialization even if already initialized\n3. Call azx_reset directly instead of azx_init_chip\n\nLooking at the code flow, option 1 seems most straightforward - just set chip->initialized = 0 in the resume path before calling azx_init_chip.\n\nThe function returns early if the chip is already marked as initialized, which prevents the reset and reinitialization sequence from running. Since the flag persists from the previous initialization, the resume path skips all the critical setup steps like azx_reset, interrupt configuration, and stream initialization. Setting the flag to 0 before resuming would allow the full initialization sequence to execute again. resuming)\n\nThe best approach is to reset polling_mode to 0 in azx_init_chip during reinitialization. Looking at the code flow, there's an early return if chip->initialized is already set, but azx_stop_chip clears this flag during suspend, so that shouldn't prevent reinitialization. The key issue is ensuring polling_mode gets cleared when the chip reinitializes after a suspend/resume cycle, since once it's set to 1 during a timeout, it persists and forces the driver into polling mode indefinitely. for changes related to polling_mode or initialization. The real issue might be in azx_init_chip itself—if chip->initialized is already set, it returns early without reinitializing. But azx_stop_chip should reset this flag, so that's not quite right either.\n\nWait, I think the actual problem is different. When switching to single_cmd mode, azx_free_cmd_io gets called to clean up the command I/O structures. On the next resume when azx_init_chip runs, those structures might not be properly reinitialized if the early return triggers or if the CORB/RIRB setup is skipped.\n\nThe sequence would be: initially polling_mode is 0 and single_cmd is 0 with CORB/RIRB working. After a timeout, polling_mode switches to 1, then single_cmd becomes 1 and azx_free_cmd_io tears down the command I/O. On suspend and resume, if the chip stays in single_cmd mode, the CORB/RIRB won't get set up again because that initialization is conditional on not being in single_cmd mode. This leaves the codec communication broken even though the driver thinks everything is initialized.\n\nThe solution is to reset polling_mode back to 0 during chip reinitialization, since this flag shouldn't carry over across suspend/resume cycles—it's meant to indicate temporary polling usage, not a persistent state. Alternatively, single_cmd could be cleared on full reset, or the command I/O initialization could be forced even in single_cmd mode during resume.","signature":"EuY+CkYICxgCKkAL/MhQWpoWToFk3+kZZL9f8A2jaE+hgqYJh/H3ta6xHdffueQa0yC0/m/2lK2HZGqf2eVpL5+lqPKFizqYcfNNEgx+CnEJoQBwNX2EGrIaDNQrWw8Njv/qPw/23iIwr3RQUz9dAeq/HB6lBJBkjONCqJxCL8NIKRSMkDQEyvVknWLOyif8lX0Sjp4ypTvkKs09gpul7ONCKbK+uijgJQ4sOSNbtIoygJev2zOHJVH8voYo7KetCC33GYl/NhQ4wYhLseUKmBjFYXkfunJC5xD9aLBLPH9VNn/+JAR7luJHzBGCFuRdj85bR8gW2GO+Y/LIZBWeGh7nu2RbnXugJN2jZGOsteh6BS4T6gw+VVDXxPwPsVy+dfRQnIUZQIL0qQAoZfQY9hY3Jpd0Ies7N78sQzs5t1JuW+fmMhpZG0ZrRMe+oL5g+C+dnWXBzQwY6OCk74cHnquVWQ0xC+CEGwk02TtNMyzDzNKbrNA7I3ddvibkUdcWoncMRkPpJmCyeeMp26R2G5fhblnFlaQkoPuLSeMqQALUbMa1WfWLlriIZFKE/TazJ4067UjhDwvbZnte2h/IJn2cEK7ZUw3avtHZ/XlSCVpRbaEG7ZwppRLlMq2355j79Cox3Da1l4/t3EoVgwaF/NYIovj9Qw78gwtyvhi2w0LPkCI6DP1DbM8Wml/oUgdmuNsYPgfbxI3eQNh3MN3Yz7K5aNqD2Zvt4/4WE9MMgv6N0XOH/7kAIOVF+1ujNStZN9dkcr+7xiwUamEVEYfXl1CYWk9QT17To+Xu9isJIEfQMmewch/6aoJGkgHWfcUPBnC7mtTTNmDG1OzVhymOVU2c3gNf7GxnU6KprzzAhH9pY69C3cn2Kk4IxRn11QEDdHdsFyjjhJ6TkGPjWnDNGwED0w63ECSvHSNiS7hQdw8ecDojE35U3ri2TH53C7Ki/7eqoiqoFa6uQmlT0nbMPb0YUrP3iJw9s67dTg6ORVm/4dwMbNzQMbleUZzZfXcfsgbsm7/WoQX2OV3koS0+8NPc85FfEZUdjeIhSeTA87xmR5v6OVm9L6NUsEUCRp7FD0voowinsXsWtuTeVoPaXlO50Jg/orUoHdEnaBh3y7Aeo8SLv4G414QAJRC9uKNqvakomT5bC3bNtBzCgEdyCKV6VvKouopi2rkzPbAprpQR2JPK5DgUXPQJejRxplmFDWSuap9XTPHdLdCIIu60QhfQMfDIFRxVDlUxstkC0qBvGwMz8lOIZSFamxL0Jxm8xRQkyaMhepf8nluaR3p4T2j280go5oqUd1uQrKyuILgQjiddJZASz2xCuIF3RXvWxDpNAcVyH/Q/nIu5iiZh7p3l5UomhABxf6ID+V32crCcbbJc+SFM1Txh+C9BnHCqI23HD512F3cdxNRFOn8jUZasOdiZUdowgrps4wk1n5fnSyaTkkLSpgcW+8MuvTd0pjA6lXymmRuB520h+hbLCR2tKzG4zo88M2ZWSoysOytFHa0X8Rxky0IuDBz4SgUK9mX9t+9s/3GBiQR2RFRshBaWPSk4d0dfEzrTRZCTbRdhFf12RHNAWREO4fViVdvQmv/AuehKlCLAuf1bTqun3eu7YWMPaIA81ZWdRT3ahyh7E5thiBYeoYfXlToW2NfH/aAZU/lqydj35KPrlnYZ2QS8ufM5IPXsMy3tAOqSURX9x39iS4Ez9tmYBnNL/6BxdH6E+omdMDy+0Dv8beGvJRG8y/ZBjjkDHzkyeWs76Tq023lDA0c5l6uRErpIngrIXZawwpownfgqpKYORf6aRJAeYhUSFJRrkydiNbQBiUXHL223rePUMS0RupA1RvTXbOH8r6nM8NCmn0tTV1u2uePNBHE5JgbIcAfT7Qm5X79zFDJz2kE9fn+D4uSV6z3kBXnFashEipw1vfsS2YzoGWgxxyGZkI/054H+O1rmzg0AruWHQxVihrGHoV {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01WCQy7HvGacF5HFehmDHrMy","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Perfect! Now I see the full picture. When the driver experiences a timeout (lines 948-957):\n1. It sets `chip->single_cmd = 1` (line 951)\n2. It calls `azx_free_cmd_io(chip)` to release CORB/RIRB (line 954)\n3. It disables unsolicited responses (line 956)\n\nThen, when the system suspends and resumes:\n1. azx_suspend calls azx_stop_chip, setting chip->initialized = 0\n2. azx_resume calls azx_init_chip, which checks if chip->initialized and has an early return\n3. In azx_init_chip, it only calls azx_init_cmd_io if `!chip->single_cmd` (line 1222-1223)\n\nSo if chip->single_cmd is still 1 after the timeout, then the CORB/RIRB won't be reinitialized during resume!\n\nBut wait, let me check more carefully. Looking at azx_init_chip:\n\n```c\nstatic void azx_init_chip(struct azx *chip, int full_reset)\n{\n    if (chip->initialized)\n        return;\n\n    /* reset controller */\n    azx_reset(chip, full_reset);\n    ...\n    if (!chip->single_cmd)\n        azx_init_cmd_io(chip);\n    ...\n    chip->initialized = 1;\n}\n```\n\nSo if chip->initialized was 0 (which it should be after azx_stop_chip), then azx_init_chip will proceed. The issue is that if chip->single_cmd is 1, then azx_init_cmd_io won't be called, so the CORB/RIRB won't be reinitialized!\n\nHowever, I also notice that polling_mode is NOT being reset in azx_init_chip. So even if CORB/RIRB are being reinitialized, if polling_mode is still 1, the driver will continue using polling mode instead of interrupt mode.\n\n\nI'm seeing two distinct problems here. First, polling_mode persists across suspend/resume cycles since nothing resets it back to 0. Second, when a timeout triggers single_cmd mode as a fallback, that flag also doesn't get cleared, which prevents CORB/RIRB reinitialization on the next resume. The comment at lines 939-940 indicates single_cmd is meant as a temporary fallback, not a permanent state. The fix likely needs to be in azx_resume to reset these flags appropriately. causing continuous codec communication failures. The fix should reset polling_mode to 0 during chip initialization, since this flag shouldn't persist across suspend/resume cycles. I also notice azx_init_chip has an early return when chip->initialized is already set, which could prevent proper reinitialization in certain scenarios. Looking at azx_stop_chip, it resets chip->initialized and calls azx_free_cmd_io, but leaves polling_mode and single_cmd flags untouched. When azx_resume later calls azx_init_chip, these stale flags remain active, breaking codec communication even after CORB/RIRB reinitialization. The best place to clear these flags is in azx_init_chip when full_reset is enabled, since that's where chip state gets restored. I should verify whether these flags are already being reset elsewhere in the code.","signature":"EuwgCkYICxgCKkCj+NvczbY7V+CZigoG9Uqa9vsZjaOwSR4ClFPFyel2UnvHv6Z6/6gcqy8jZhHYlds7Qf2od5pOS3w6im8N13gSEgyMTQhUnfP6Oc0V/V4aDNltFWg+idIiFx+ahiIwoFj+pUWGsg66Wt4x02QJTwbE7hK/Mwm7xxLVNqiYTCIO8JXOJGrPPMfD2DzZaa37KtMfMHu+qoFQFIaGsewobPVj0/Go/ubK4MV9gO15KdFqafE1jeELik8bBVtSAnQftU2p8m2j/L4HOelUDcbk6KycrlriLCQke/TtxxXVniHpxuz9Q7SxWjlBeXNuQWAm8S8GI43sroaeb1U/eaFPAGb4MYltZ28d99SFlTTk8+dQF5W03me9zn7PZe/9VLD1unJheeVXjOiGtxJLmhy1QQM/gDa5Xy9isqMqXu6LKRDSk9c1oQC64gXrZ6jh3CtI8qsx8cfIe6Uzmhlto0nTIEnBw+ruAMMZ1IMqE0GmDMvJdPol+gI6lmvC1c7rDgd9Q5cq9W+LGMlttja7eXkHcr2+yzf6l9qYVLnbIAI7NKMKMahx+MblIQz9XA8KpiKm+8p7oEQDZa8p/7H42n7VfwpKUq/URAhmzXCn/dYKV9HWFzDFBPLaDO6A7pmCC2U3+/22ji6g7V1c5BoDk1j7Rq03t/JLhrc7BRmmd6pgRsCBVgVk+7UlBxtcrFbmKl5aovNsU7Vs+UYnh/xHsXkOPQfHjBjLPxvjGGnfhnW+lm8Bn+kYv13P8D7Cuw1MePo/bog4m+qpomBBD6bW4nOBLCi/Lj4o5BBtG3UI5jrQS6CwMZ1ZDf1K1v56xp/ChFODgXDeeYpR2XaALss5iUaghJMzcNVob/dtOOvC4vz2l9raeaUqqCH8Prob8CPiJ3lD3Nb8F1JFU/7jDCzwA4QlTYEwTDSP7YD7+mQPPPkZiMjLJ+G43tBUEX4gDT8dALBbgVBzNv7GNzfyxBDmIrrAUzJuUcEKmvsVcd3yaCfdIRHeGx18MmC4gnQVy8PUnCa/l+e+jJPZREd0O26K0bML+UiZvMf6qRDRNPYw4nH6QhzvyIvAbQx33paAvaDE6+Y2PypX+IiWgCP38s32oMEZ+U2q+FKyILhXSOKWv10o4ivEwMQVtKUhbyisnmfhan6HUIpKSa/BJq/Y2FwDBUVd+MYI0A0rCoggR40FVLf3Jh7torBgNWvtZhkEHXlZ7Up3I47nR6AlDEPuhrWjnFFOlqTWIQHSJo06IXBYnZPAtHaO8JRbFZrvFBL3mOX1Ixd91lF/Kp1cSRCb11dApGLTZbsQSEwnsrLu9mcgb+Yw2+mzhH74olWT9DBZzEpiCx80TZ3Z03mcpZ5mRIAx7WKvBIHDkr2XS5V8NXCHSpn83D3oz/5sGPMhNgNdYUXngZGfVLRfKUYANLhNKbCf3nZoCmMLk12Ad/AeaDFUEEu7FN63dQPMTzleABmTTlCye7trunBzg6FGWREQaYmcDjivr/kVskkWrdmSo3demrhPvMdK1rAYhnDj0bgoIylhtYvAqrz0J+vjhhsbfoyb5Jfcwgg4rzTIKeCGc02M26G+6h5e7SsNw6J9lUrpsFVxPTG0GG4b5mgRCsgheSINXEg7iWeSzffQrwCfIm+c2lWpMXGJODg3oOUCbH3s/nV8rUqiDa1L7xTqbzY1AZPWFxmzBthYdD54JUUPyIz1uxHfX12nu5YSHHegPd49G99LheD5av4SbZHTWIBi50WkXVKIBIlkHTBX1BxfLuyH9JSRQSahUXHF4VJ+tnRWy58cwKd5ojkToh0/F6vdMcs1JKxs9YYsJMJS4c+vKU90snX8PTiN7+GPxSoBpW9bHJfHi7ao2SqyrlGVnScGKlLZrEvU+3QXdXH7Aj4M0KDd9wiZS5z9ISB86t2Url5VTKIAmLYncbPCdqbHtq3Tdp64pF5tnzcIPBQwcUdKJ6HZoTOviTqZiXOZ
